  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer12030096213261564044">There are many things that Annah would like to forget: the look on her sister's face before Annah left her behind in the Forest of Hands and Teeth, her first glimpse of the Horde as they swarmed the Dark City, the sear of the barbed wire that would scar her for life. But most of all, Annah would like to forget the morning Elias left her for the Recruiters.  <br/>Annah's world s</span>
  <span id="freeText12030096213261564044" style="display:none">There are many things that Annah would like to forget: the look on her sister's face before Annah left her behind in the Forest of Hands and Teeth, her first glimpse of the Horde as they swarmed the Dark City, the sear of the barbed wire that would scar her for life. But most of all, Annah would like to forget the morning Elias left her for the Recruiters.  <br />Annah's world stopped that day, and she's been waiting for Elias to come home ever since. Somehow, without him, her life doesn't feel much different than the dead that roam the wasted city around her. Until she meets Catcher, and everything feels alive again. <br />But Catcher has his own secrets. Dark, terrifying truths that link him to a past Annah has longed to forget, and to a future too deadly to consider. And now it's up to Annah: can she continue to live in a world covered in the blood of the living? Or is death the only escape from the Return's destruction?</span>
  <a data-text-id="12030096213261564044" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<div id="review_162860210" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/162860210" />
    <a title="⋟Kiki⋞" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3555205-kiki"><img alt="⋟Kiki⋞" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1390274805p2/3555205.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/162860210?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="⋟Kiki⋞" class="user" itemprop="url" name="⋟Kiki⋞" href="/user/show/3555205-kiki">⋟Kiki⋞</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780375895593" href="/book/show/10517010-the-dark-and-hollow-places">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3555205-kiki?shelf=united-states">united-states</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3555205-kiki?shelf=romance-ensues">romance-ensues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3555205-kiki?shelf=survival">survival</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3555205-kiki?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3555205-kiki?shelf=post-apocalyptic">post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3555205-kiki?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3555205-kiki?shelf=undead">undead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3555205-kiki?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer162860210" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10206061516585993536">After <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/122656098' rel='nofollow noopener'>reading and reviewing</a> The Dead Tossed Waves, I wasn't planning on reading the final book in this series. But, I hate starting a series and not finishing it, and I really hoped this book would be better. <br/><br/>The plot follows the previous two books; there's the whiny, self-pitying girl, the love triangle, and the need to escape. The writing hasn't improved either. Something is always almost like something else, unimaginative similes abound. Someone is always retching or vomiting. When hands, fin</span>
  <span id="freeText10206061516585993536" style="display:none">After <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/122656098" rel="nofollow noopener">reading and reviewing</a> The Dead Tossed Waves, I wasn't planning on reading the final book in this series. But, I hate starting a series and not finishing it, and I really hoped this book would be better. <br /><br />The plot follows the previous two books; there's the whiny, self-pitying girl, the love triangle, and the need to escape. The writing hasn't improved either. Something is always almost like something else, unimaginative similes abound. Someone is always retching or vomiting. When hands, fingers, or knuckles are mentioned, they're raw, ragged, bloody, or bruised. Throats and voices are raw and ragged too. If you need an adjective, any adjective, just use one of these four.<br /><br />Annah is always whining about her scars and hiding behind her hair. It makes her look meek. Instead of being invisible, she stands out as an easy target. Like Catcher, I was tired of having her 'badge' thrown in my face. It's her personality and her refusal to open up, not her scars, that makes her ugly. <br /><br />In contrast, Gabry is more mature and steady. She's much more likable than in the previous book. Catcher and Elias are nice guys, even if they're not very multi-dimensional. The remaining characters were just filler, bad guy #1, bad guy #2, victim #1, etc. No personality or motives needed.<br /><br />This could have been a 2 star book, except for one thing. The escape at the end is <i>beyond</i> ridiculous. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[An armada of hot air balloons made from ragged old quilts and clothing? I'm still laughing.<br /><br />To have enough lift for 3 people and a supply of firewood, the airbag would need to hold approximately 2,500 cubic meters of hot air. It seems improbably that Annah would have found enough nylon or silk to construct even a single balloon. Cotton, polyester, or wool wouldn't work, the fabric is too stretchy and heavy. The inconsistency of a wood fire, coupled with the danger of sparks igniting the oiled cloth, probably wouldn't have been a success either. There were no test flights, no modification to the design. Nothing. It's hard to believe that dozens of these balloons were constructed in secret, or that any of them were air-worthy.<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />If you liked this series, you might also enjoy:<br /><br />✱ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/43930-the-clockwork-century" rel="nofollow noopener">The Clockwork Century</a> series</span>
  <a data-text-id="10206061516585993536" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_160703834" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/160703834" />
    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/160703834?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Sinclair" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair">Steph Sinclair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2011-reads">2011-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=i-really-enjoyed-it">i-really-enjoyed-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=i-loved-it">i-loved-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=original-and-creative">original-and-creative</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=zombies-zombies-everywhere">zombies-zombies-everywhere</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer160703834" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7235418111987207878"><br/>You know how when you are reading a book and you can sort of tell when the author lets her characters off the hook or saves them from a potentially devastating situation? Well, Carrie Ryan spares no sort of mercy for her characters. In fact, she leaves your soul begging for a way out for them. I found myself bargaining with Ryan to please cut them some slack! But Alas, such is not the way in any of the Forest of Hands and Teeth novels. While the POV changed from each of the three books, one cons</span>
  <span id="freeText7235418111987207878" style="display:none"><br>You know how when you are reading a book and you can sort of tell when the author lets her characters off the hook or saves them from a potentially devastating situation? Well, Carrie Ryan spares no sort of mercy for her characters. In fact, she leaves your soul begging for a way out for them. I found myself bargaining with Ryan to please cut them some slack! But Alas, such is not the way in any of the Forest of Hands and Teeth novels. While the POV changed from each of the three books, one constant always remained:<br><br> <a href="http://s181.photobucket.com/albums/x95/shellnick2003/Mobile%20Uploads/?action=view&amp;current=Zombies.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380348316i/702593._SX540_.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Or the “Unconsecrated,” “Mudo,” or “Plague Rats” depending which book you’re on. <br><br>The Dark and Hollow Places (or the series in general) is epic. I can honestly say I really, really liked it, perhaps even loved it. However, it is not an adventure I would want to read again. It is just too damn depressing. And I’ll probably have Zombie filled dreams the next night I sleep. The world Ryan creates is so grim, so full of darkness and despair. Honestly, its awesome. It feels like you are watching a horror movie. <br><br>The book picks up with Gabry’s twin sister, Annah. What a broken character! At first, I thought Annah was sure to annoy the hell out of me with her constant complaints of her scars. But she quickly grew on me. Annah is a very strong, solid, female protagonist. Is she flawed? Sure. She is so used to depending on herself for everything, that she is afraid to let anyone get close to her. Throughout the novel, she learns that if she or her loved ones are going to make it, she has to learn to trust again. <br><br>Annah can not take a break in this novel. Ryan puts her through some pretty hellish situations that left me doing something like this: <a href="http://s181.photobucket.com/albums/x95/shellnick2003/Mobile%20Uploads/?action=view&amp;current=1302994761.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380348316ra/702594.gif" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> Or this: <a href="http://s181.photobucket.com/albums/x95/shellnick2003/Mobile%20Uploads/?action=view&amp;current=1302994750.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380348316i/702595.gif" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> I was on the edge of my seat for most of the book. Nowhere was safe, not from the Zombies or the recruiters. Many times they all just wanted to give up. But really, who could blame them? Ryan brought up a very good question in this book: What is the difference from surviving and simply existing? What do you do when you only have a short time to live? Well, you LIVE. You continuing fighting, feeling, believing. <br><br>So, if you haven’t read this book or series…what are you waiting for?! The Return?! <br><br>More reviews and more at <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery Book Blog</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7235418111987207878" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_161775898" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/161775898" />
    <a title="Wendy Darling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling"><img alt="Wendy Darling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379959930p2/2745288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/161775898?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy Darling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy Darling" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=dystopian-post-apocalyptic-utopian">dystopian-post-apocalyptic-utopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=pn-zombies-biters">pn-zombies-biters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer161775898" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7533038152871475085">I really liked <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3432478.The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth__The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth___1_' title='The Forest of Hands and Teeth (The Forest of Hands and Teeth, #1) by Carrie Ryan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Forest of Hands and Teeth</a>, which I thought was a bleak, well-written take on the whole zombie story. I wasn't as big a fan of the follow-up novel, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6555517.The_Dead_Tossed_Waves__The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth___2_' title='The Dead-Tossed Waves (The Forest of Hands and Teeth, #2) by Carrie Ryan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dead-Tossed Waves</a>, primarily because I thought Gabry was a bit of a whiner and a little too obsessed with boys in the middle of all the death, dying, and undead. <br/><br/>As such, I wasn't sure whether I was eager to follow the story with the third installment in the series, but happily The Dark and Hollow Places returns with a compellin</span>
  <span id="freeText7533038152871475085" style="display:none">I really liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3432478.The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth__The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth___1_" title="The Forest of Hands and Teeth (The Forest of Hands and Teeth, #1) by Carrie Ryan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Forest of Hands and Teeth</a>, which I thought was a bleak, well-written take on the whole zombie story. I wasn't as big a fan of the follow-up novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6555517.The_Dead_Tossed_Waves__The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth___2_" title="The Dead-Tossed Waves (The Forest of Hands and Teeth, #2) by Carrie Ryan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dead-Tossed Waves</a>, primarily because I thought Gabry was a bit of a whiner and a little too obsessed with boys in the middle of all the death, dying, and undead. <br /><br />As such, I wasn't sure whether I was eager to follow the story with the third installment in the series, but happily The Dark and Hollow Places returns with a compellingly flawed narrator in Annah, Gabry's long-lost twin. A frightened and lonely child who grows up to be a scarred and mistrustful woman, Annah is much more interesting than her sheltered twin--and Catcher, who was part of the triangle in the last book, is much more appealing than Elias. As with the previous books there's a lot of running away from the Unconsecrated, hiding out in forests, and fighting off unwanted attention.<br /><br />I would preferred to have seen Annah come to accept herself in a more obvious way, to have had a little more time spent on her relationship with Catcher (it felt a little too close for comfort to have her pining for <i>both</i> of her sister's lovers), and I still don't really understand why authors ever want to write in the present tense. But overall the story moves along at a fast clip with descriptive narration and some pretty cool action sequences. There's a fairly open-ended close to the novel, but being that there are finally some notes of hope in this dark world, I'm kind of hoping that this is the end of the series. Better to let it finish on a high note than to let it drag out interminably.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7533038152871475085" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_112673152" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/112673152" />
    <a title="Megan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1233686-megan"><img alt="Megan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1334791106p2/1233686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/112673152?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan" href="/user/show/1233686-megan">Megan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1233686-megan?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1233686-megan?shelf=zombies">zombies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1233686-megan?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer112673152" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5298313516261082698">Perhaps I need to go back and reread <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6468718.The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth__The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth___1_' title='The Forest of Hands and Teeth (The Forest of Hands and Teeth, #1) by Carrie Ryan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Forest of Hands and Teeth</a>. The thing is, that book blew me away. I loved the mystery, the surreal quality, Mary's craziness, the pervading sense of doom and of course the never ending onslaught of the Unconsecrated. I remember reading the book late at night, in the middle of a storm while the hubby was away. Between the wind and lightening I could hear moans of the undead, and when thunder shook my old, isolated house I imagined hoards at my door. I was s</span>
  <span id="freeText5298313516261082698" style="display:none">Perhaps I need to go back and reread <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6468718.The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth__The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth___1_" title="The Forest of Hands and Teeth (The Forest of Hands and Teeth, #1) by Carrie Ryan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Forest of Hands and Teeth</a>. The thing is, that book blew me away. I loved the mystery, the surreal quality, Mary's craziness, the pervading sense of doom and of course the never ending onslaught of the Unconsecrated. I remember reading the book late at night, in the middle of a storm while the hubby was away. Between the wind and lightening I could hear moans of the undead, and when thunder shook my old, isolated house I imagined hoards at my door. I was so spooked that I actually had to put the book down and take a break from it! Carrie Ryan can write a creepy zombie story that is for sure. <br /><br />Needless to say, I was completely let down by the teen angst portrayed in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6555517.The_Dead_Tossed_Waves__The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth___2_" title="The Dead-Tossed Waves (The Forest of Hands and Teeth, #2) by Carrie Ryan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dead-Tossed Waves</a>, almost so much so that I considered not continuing with the final installment of this trilogy. But of course I did finally read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8535273.The_Dark_and_Hollow_Places__The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth___3_" title="The Dark and Hollow Places (The Forest of Hands and Teeth, #3) by Carrie Ryan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dark and Hollow Places</a>. The verdict? Well, Carrie Ryan can still write some of the best zombie scenes ever. So many zombie books fail because they go for the immediate scare and shock value. But Ryan manages to build up a slow tension and throughout the novel and allow the reader to truly see the hopelessness and horror of a zombie apocalypse.<br /><br /><i>And then they come, stumbling from the cloud of dust and dirt: Unconsecrated. At fist it’s just a few, but then there are more and more, struggling across the rubble and flooding into the streets. Slow but steady they flow like blood from a seeping wound. <br />Some are short and some are tall. Some men and others women. Some wear clothes from olden times and some are naked, their bodies striped with wounds. But all moan with gaping black mouths. All claw at the air, reaching and needing. Some of them shuffle on broken limbs, arms gnawed away, with stringy gray tendons swinging with each step. <br />There are more than I could ever count and I know this is just the beginning. Soon the entire City will fall to them. I stare and wonder how we’ve survived as long as we have against such an inevitable destruction.</i><br /><br />Unfortunately, Ryan also has a desire to write about teenage angst and lurve. While this worked well in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6468718.The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth__The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth___1_" title="The Forest of Hands and Teeth (The Forest of Hands and Teeth, #1) by Carrie Ryan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Forest of Hands and Teeth</a>, it’s old hat by now. At this point the zombie scenes and the supporting characters are meant only to hinder the romance and heighten the angst. Teenagers talk philosophically about the nature of life, love and death and manage to be the only good guys amongst many of the survivors we encounter. *yawn* <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8535273.The_Dark_and_Hollow_Places__The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth___3_" title="The Dark and Hollow Places (The Forest of Hands and Teeth, #3) by Carrie Ryan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dark and Hollow Places</a> is a solid three stars for me. While I absolutely love Ryan’s ideas and writing style, her execution of this trilogy leaves something to be desired. I would love to see her break away from a plot which is so dependent on the lurve and the angst. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5298313516261082698" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_172541878" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/172541878" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310159877p2/4800103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/172541878?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer172541878" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18184738364138421434">This is definitely the best of the three. Just as original and thought provoking as the first two in the series- in The Dark and Hollow Places we follow yet a new character, Annah, as the protagonist. Although the others from The Dead-Tossed Waves are present as well. Some more than others, but don't fret- you won't miss anyone; Annah's story is plenty interesting. I also found her to be a much more competent main character than Mary and Gabry. She is strong and self sufficient. I really admired</span>
  <span id="freeText18184738364138421434" style="display:none">This is definitely the best of the three. Just as original and thought provoking as the first two in the series- in The Dark and Hollow Places we follow yet a new character, Annah, as the protagonist. Although the others from The Dead-Tossed Waves are present as well. Some more than others, but don't fret- you won't miss anyone; Annah's story is plenty interesting. I also found her to be a much more competent main character than Mary and Gabry. She is strong and self sufficient. I really admired her determination and will to live.<br /><br />In addition to its originality, we still run and hide, escaping the Unconsecrated, fighting for our lives in this exhilarating pulse pounding conclusion. Although the ending is still a bit open-ended with room for more books in the future, I'd be fine if this was it. It's a perfect way to end this series: Hopeful and believable.<br /><br />There is no slow start in this third novel. We are thrown right in at high speeds that don't slow down until the last page. It's easily the darkest book in the series. The Unconsecrated are not the only enemy anymore, and I don't know which is worse. We really see the lengths that people will go to in order to survive. Some even make the zombies seem charming. Regardless of all this horror, we've still got some love and romance to gush through. The chemistry between the characters is much more present which makes it easier to root for them.<br /><br />It's all brilliantly written. The settings, the different protagonists, the passion, the helplessness, the hope, it adds up to give a very realistic world. It made my adrenaline pump and my heart ache. I thoroughly enjoyed it all. I also have to mention that the covers are gorgeous!! That alone is worth having these on your shelves! <br /><br />--<br />For more of my reviews, visit my blog at <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>Xpresso Reads</b>
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="18184738364138421434" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15700386208340709494"><b>*4.5 UNDEAD STARS*</b><br/><br/>Screw <i>The Walking Dead</i>, if there's ever a zombie apocalypse, I want to be like Annah!<br/><br/><b>
  <i>"Life is never that simple. And the fact that it's not that simple to you means only one thing: you're still alive."</i>
</b><br/><br/>This book was by far the best one in this entire series and I'm kind of mad at myself for leaving two years between reading the first two and this one. I would've enjoyed this one so much more right after the other two because this really brought all the storylines together ni</span>
  <span id="freeText15700386208340709494" style="display:none"><b>*4.5 UNDEAD STARS*</b><br /><br />Screw <i>The Walking Dead</i>, if there's ever a zombie apocalypse, I want to be like Annah!<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"Life is never that simple. And the fact that it's not that simple to you means only one thing: you're still alive."</i>
</b><br /><br />This book was by far the best one in this entire series and I'm kind of mad at myself for leaving two years between reading the first two and this one. I would've enjoyed this one so much more right after the other two because this really brought all the storylines together nicely! It finally all made sense now! Book 1 was about Mary. Book 2 about Mary's daughter Gabry and this one was about Gabry's twin sister Annah and included pretty much all the characters from the previous books, still trying to survive in a world full of <i>Unconsecrated</i>.<br /><br />I really don't get why these books aren't more popular! These already draw you in by their <b>haunting</b> titles! And don't get me wrong, these are definitely <b>not</b> everyone's cup of tea. They're extremely <i>dark</i> and made me question humanity more than once. <br />I felt hopeless in Annah's place because of all she had to go through, but she was headstrong and never gave up! I admire that about her and I wish I was more like her in that aspect. I probably would've been dead literally 0.5 seconds after the zombie outbreak started lol, I'm just that clumsy. She also literally managed to find love in a hopeless place. (<s>eat that, Rihanna!</s>)<br />By the way, Catcher, I still love you and you know it!</span>

<div id="review_94983501" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/94983501" />
    <a title="Krys" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2798856-krys"><img alt="Krys" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1329103793p2/2798856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/94983501?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Krys" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Krys" href="/user/show/2798856-krys">Krys</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=dystopian-post-apocalyptic">dystopian-post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=monster-hunting">monster-hunting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=horror-thriller">horror-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=zombies">zombies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=autographed">autographed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798856-krys?shelf=first-person-narrative">first-person-narrative</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer94983501" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2213834069733587844"><br/>I've been slowly working through The Dark and Hollow Places by Carrie Ryan for the last couple of days. Partly, I blame the stupidity of ongoing health dramas. Partly I blame myself. This is "the final" book in the trilogy... and I simply did not want to let these books go.<br/><br/>The Dark and Hollow Places starts out with a new character - Annah, the twin sister of Gabry from book two. Annah lives in the Dark City and is patiently awaiting the return of Elias, who went off to find Annah's sister, Abiga</span>
  <span id="freeText2213834069733587844" style="display:none"><br />I've been slowly working through The Dark and Hollow Places by Carrie Ryan for the last couple of days. Partly, I blame the stupidity of ongoing health dramas. Partly I blame myself. This is "the final" book in the trilogy... and I simply did not want to let these books go.<br /><br />The Dark and Hollow Places starts out with a new character - Annah, the twin sister of Gabry from book two. Annah lives in the Dark City and is patiently awaiting the return of Elias, who went off to find Annah's sister, Abigail. Annah and Elias left Abigail behind in the Forest of Hands and Teeth ten years ago while fleeing the Unconsecrated. Since then Annah has regretted the decision every day. Her guilt is visibly represented on her flesh by severe scars, an accident caused by barbed wire. Annah thinks of her sister and knows that she herself is ugly.<br /><br />Three people come into the city that irrevocably change Annah's life. One is Elias, the man Annah is in love with. Another is Gabry, Annah's sister, who is in love with Elias as well. The third is Catcher, the Immune former flame of Gabry. All three of these characters serve as a symbolic counterpoint for Annah in provocative ways. They also make a very impacting point in the story. Because of Catcher's immunity the Recruiters (who secure the defenses in Dark City) have forced him to infiltrate the infected areas for supplies. To keep him in line they imprison Annah, Gabry, and Elias but they really only need to keep one alive to maintain Catcher's loyalty. The threat of their deaths are ever-present in (and out) of Dark City.<br /><br />I really like what Ryan did with this book. Granted, it took me a minute to get into the storyline but once Gabry and co. made their presence known I was hooked. Annah is a hard character to wrap your brain around. I wasn't convinced, at first, that I was going to like her voice. I wasn't sure I was ready for her darkness. She's a completely different character than the first two women; her inner strength comes from years of self-loathing more than success. I was scared of how dark she was in the beginning, but I quickly grew to appreciate her, to love her. I really grew to love her.<br /><br />This is, potentially, the darkest book in the series. But it's not because of the dead, it's because of the living. The things that people do, the things that people become in order to survive, are truly monstrous, and Ryan drives this home with efficient grace. It's not the undead we need fear, it's ourselves. Beautifully, masterfully done.<br /><br />I'm really glad that I had this book to read this week. Really. Very. Glad.<br /><br />5 out of 5 stars. It's bittersweet to see this series end, but I'm very happy with the final book.<br /><br />- review courtesy of <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bibliopunkkreads.com">www.bibliopunkkreads.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2213834069733587844" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2885175166186748277">The first book in this series "The Forest of Hands and Teeth" was such a great story, then the second book "The Dead Tossed Waves" wasn't really a sequel, it was a whole different story with mostly different characters and it didn't make references to the first book very often, so you didn’t get any answers to the questions that the first book raised. This last book "The Dark and Hollow Places" is a sequel to "The Dead Tossed Waves", I started skimming about mid book because I thought it was get</span>
  <span id="freeText2885175166186748277" style="display:none">The first book in this series "The Forest of Hands and Teeth" was such a great story, then the second book "The Dead Tossed Waves" wasn't really a sequel, it was a whole different story with mostly different characters and it didn't make references to the first book very often, so you didn’t get any answers to the questions that the first book raised. This last book "The Dark and Hollow Places" is a sequel to "The Dead Tossed Waves", I started skimming about mid book because I thought it was getting a little bit boring and repetitive. There wasn't much of a big finale, and it didn't really go in the direction I thought it would, it just sort of faded into an ending, "and they rode off into the sunset" sort of a thing. Very inconclusive, and very disappointing. </span>

<div id="review_133131586" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/133131586" />
    <a title="Mundie Moms &amp; Mundie Kids" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4397975-mundie-moms-mundie-kids"><img alt="Mundie Moms &amp; Mundie Kids" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1319228268p2/4397975.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/133131586?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mundie Moms &amp; Mundie Kids" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mundie Moms &amp; Mundie Kids" href="/user/show/4397975-mundie-moms-mundie-kids">Mundie Moms &amp; Mundie Kids</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4397975-mundie-moms-mundie-kids?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4397975-mundie-moms-mundie-kids?shelf=2011-release">2011-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4397975-mundie-moms-mundie-kids?shelf=2011-100-book-challenge">2011-100-book-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4397975-mundie-moms-mundie-kids?shelf=mundie-moms-reviews">mundie-moms-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4397975-mundie-moms-mundie-kids?shelf=signed-books-arcs">signed-books-arcs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer133131586" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11882783411214878385">Carrie Ryan has a talent for writing. Not only does her writing increase in perfection with each book, but she creates a world that feels so real while reading it, that I hopelessly and willingly fall victim to it's brilliance. Yes I know zombies aren't real, but they sure feel real when you're reading Carrie's series. I can honestly say I am NOT a zombie fan, but I'm a die hard Carrie Ryan zombie fan. There's a difference, as Carrie's main characters are not zombies, but the world in which they</span>
  <span id="freeText11882783411214878385" style="display:none">Carrie Ryan has a talent for writing. Not only does her writing increase in perfection with each book, but she creates a world that feels so real while reading it, that I hopelessly and willingly fall victim to it's brilliance. Yes I know zombies aren't real, but they sure feel real when you're reading Carrie's series. I can honestly say I am NOT a zombie fan, but I'm a die hard Carrie Ryan zombie fan. There's a difference, as Carrie's main characters are not zombies, but the world in which they live is over run with them.<br /><br />The Dark and Hollow Places lives up to it's name and is the darker of the three, but it also made it the most realistic. Without giving away any spoilers, what happens with the characters in the story wasn't shocking to me and is something that fits a story who's world is facing an end. This is something that felt real and something I can see really happening, as human nature takes over. People either fight to survive or become barbaric and let me just say that a few of the Recruiters make the zombies look nice.<br /><br />What I've loved about this series is that each book is from a different character's point of view, and each story is told in manner that I not only get to see the characters in a variety of ways, but also their world. What I loved most with this story is the way in which Carrie brings all her characters together and wraps up her series. The Dark and Hollow Places is told from Annah's point of view, Gabry's twin sister. I really enjoyed getting to know Annah, and I loved the romance that grows between her and Catcher. It's so broken, and hopeful all at the same time and filled with tension, which I love. I really fell in love with Catcher in TDTW, but this time his desperation is so much more urgent that I really wanted to reach out to him. Annah and Catcher mold together perfectly, as they're the only ones who are able to really understand each other. I'm so glad that Gabry and Elias were apart of the story, but this time they were great supporting characters.<br /><br />The setting in which the story takes place really helps set the tone and feel of the book. Dark City is overrun and falling apart and it's the last strong hold survivors have. The darkened subway tunnels are beyond creepy! My adrenaline started running while reading these scenes they're that creepy, but so fitting for the story. While the setting makes the world and the story feel helpless, the characters give it hope, which was so appealing to me. Annah for me is the essence of survival. Her passion for living really brought the story to life. She often questions the way in which she was changing and how could she not? She's had to deal with some pretty horrific things both from what she's seen and experienced. She won't give up, even when all seems lost.<br /><br />I truly loved the moments I spent being apart of the world Carrie created. With The Dark and Hollow Place I had a few of those "ah ha" moments when Carrie ties together her previous two story lines, and adds them to this story's deliciously twisted plot. And oh what an ending! It's biter sweet, hopeful, and exactly how a series should end. If you have not picked up Carrie's series, I highly recommend it. The Dark and Hollow Places is a must have book and I recommend running out today to pick up.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11882783411214878385" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_95679331" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/95679331" />
    <a title="Penny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/679025-penny"><img alt="Penny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1323234939p2/679025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/95679331?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Penny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Penny" href="/user/show/679025-penny">Penny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer95679331" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10196269666032955484">Brief-ish summary (that isn't so much spoilery as it is more of a quick set-up of the plot during the first chapter or so): Teenage Annah has been on her own for three years, since Elias--the boy with whom she got lost in the forest several years prior--left to join the protectorate to secure a better future for both of them. In the Dark City where lawlessness prevails Annah learned quickly what it takes to fend for herself. She's had to be strong in order to survive. <br/><br/>Because of street smarts an</span>
  <span id="freeText10196269666032955484" style="display:none">Brief-ish summary (that isn't so much spoilery as it is more of a quick set-up of the plot during the first chapter or so): Teenage Annah has been on her own for three years, since Elias--the boy with whom she got lost in the forest several years prior--left to join the protectorate to secure a better future for both of them. In the Dark City where lawlessness prevails Annah learned quickly what it takes to fend for herself. She's had to be strong in order to survive. <br /><br />Because of street smarts and childhood accident that left part of her face and body marred Annah's been fortunate to fend off creepers and the like. Unfortunately the very same scars cause Annah to keep everyone at arms length. She walks the streets with her head down, speaking only when necessary and has no friends or acquaintances. She's literally all on her own as she waits for Elias to return to her. <br /><br />Near the beginning of The Dark and Hollow Places Annah makes the decision to move on--Elias has been gone three years when he only signed up for two. She knows that there is a good chance he's dead or worse. She knows it's foolish to continue living in the same building they lived in together as it's been declared unsafe and the city is getting more dangerous every day. <br /><br />It's when she's leaving the city for what's supposed to be the last time she sees a teenage girl who has her face, or rather the face she would have were it not for all the scars. Annah knows without a doubt the girl is her long-lost identical twin, Abigail, whom she and Elias left in the forest all those years ago. Guilt-stricken, there hasn't been a day in which Annah hasn't thought about Abigail, about her fate--whether she found her way back to their village or not. <br /><br />Annah attempts to get to Abigail who, ironically enough, is entering the Dark City. She fails because of the excessive, though entirely necessary security measures in place. Helplessly she watches Abigail pass by, hoping she can locate her after she returns to the city. Around the same time a young man, also entering the city, becomes the focus of nearly everybody's attention when security dogs start barking at him, identifying him as infected. Turns out Abigail is traveling with the young man and helps him escape from the peacekeepers. In turn they take her into custody while Annah looks on, horrified. <br /><br />And this, folks, is when things get truly interesting but I'm going to have to finish reviewing this book later as my five year old needs attention <u>RIGHT NOW</u>! (Seriously, the world might just end if I don't do her bidding.)<br /><br />----<br /><br />Original short review:<br /><br />More like 3.9 stars but I went ahead and rounded it up because it is the series finale and it ended well. The protagonist is the strongest Ryan has written to-date, though a little too much of a tortured soul from time to time. There are times in which I found myself choking on her pain, which isn't necessarily a bad thing. <br /><br />It's just that Ryan writes heartbreak and rejection so well, I found myself sort of reliving some of the nastier, best-left-forgotten experiences from my adolescence. I was choking on bitterness on the MC's behalf and I even hated the 'other girl'. So glad I'm no longer a teenager, but I digress.<br /><br />I'll write a full review when I get to my computer as typing this out from a phone isn't very fun.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10196269666032955484" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_96871334" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/96871334" />
    <a title="usagi ☆ミ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1101220-usagi"><img alt="usagi ☆ミ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415168132p2/1101220.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/96871334?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="usagi ☆ミ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="usagi ☆ミ" href="/user/show/1101220-usagi">usagi ☆ミ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1101220-usagi?shelf=best-of-11">best-of-11</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1101220-usagi?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1101220-usagi?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1101220-usagi?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1101220-usagi?shelf=own-finished-copy">own-finished-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1101220-usagi?shelf=zombies">zombies</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer96871334" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9430128581829370304">Picking up right where we left off at the end of "The Dead-Tossed Waves", "The Dark and Hollow Places" ups the pace of the story, making us feel just as desperate as the rest of the main characters thus far.<br/><br/>This last third book in the trilogy (though I really, really hope there are others!) unites all of the characters we've met since the first book together in a frenetic union of panic and love, lust and hurt. Annah's love of her sister combined with the hate that springs forth once she learns </span>
  <span id="freeText9430128581829370304" style="display:none">Picking up right where we left off at the end of "The Dead-Tossed Waves", "The Dark and Hollow Places" ups the pace of the story, making us feel just as desperate as the rest of the main characters thus far.<br /><br />This last third book in the trilogy (though I really, really hope there are others!) unites all of the characters we've met since the first book together in a frenetic union of panic and love, lust and hurt. Annah's love of her sister combined with the hate that springs forth once she learns how Abagail/Gabry grew up is a tasty treat, sweet and sour, to be enjoyed slowly as it simmers to a head near the middle of the book. Just as the first book was Mary's story and the second was Gabry's, make no mistake that this last story in the trilogy belongs to Annah and Ryan never lets us forget that. We're deeply immersed in Annah and her psyche the entire time, and how she fights with herself on whether she loves or hates her sister, Catcher, and Elias.<br /><br />Between this and the panic spurred on by the actions of Catcher, Elias, and Gabry at the end of the previous book, it feels like you're on a marathon - heart pounding, lactic acid in your legs the entire time. And it burns - teenage love in the middle of a world that's ending. <br /><br />But it burns so, so good. Ryan has only honed and perfected her craft of agonized teenage affection throughout all three books, which is really well represented in this last story. <br /><br />And then there's the generational aspect as well; Mary's story was the first story, somewhere around 20 years previous to the second book. By the end of this third book, you get the feeling that things have come full circle, that there is hope, another generation to be born, and even though they may have to fight for their lives, they WILL live.<br /><br />That, ultimately, I think is Ryan's message: if there's life there's hope, and if there's hope, there's love. And that's what makes us different from the dead, just as Annah says in the book - the fact that we're aware and fight for these emotions makes us alive, makes us fallible, but makes us human. This is the line that separates us from the dead.<br /><br />I really hope there are more books in the world of "Hands and Teeth" - "Hare Moon", a novella just released online (which I haven't had a chance to read yet), apparently also takes place in the same universe. But I'd like a prequel, maybe something to answer what happened to cause the Return, or a sequel/separate trilogy of what happened after this last book. I won't take no for an answer.<br /><br />This one's in my top five for 2011 so far, and the year's not even over yet. Simply gorgeous.<br /><br />(crossposted to librarything, shelfari, and witchoftheatregoing.wordpress.com) </span>
  <a data-text-id="9430128581829370304" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vee_Bookish // YA Book Blogger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vee_Bookish // YA Book Blogger" href="/user/show/67389898-vee-bookish-ya-book-blogger">Vee_Bookish // YA Book Blogger</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780575094833" href="/book/show/10494773-the-dark-and-hollow-places-the-forest-of-hands-and-teeth-3">review of another edition</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3027350249" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer5218531964817903270">I'm also a book blogger: <a href='https://vee-bookish.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Vee_Bookish</a><br/><br/>Honestly, this book made slogging through the first two worth it. While Mary and Gabry (Annah's twin sister) spend most of their time whining and letting everyone else fix things for them, Annah seemed much more independent after being left in the Dark City by Elias three years ago. She's by far my favourite character of the three girls and really made the read worthwhile, particularly towards the final pages.<br/><br/>Elias and Gabry did not come across as well however</span>
  <span id="freeText5218531964817903270" style="display:none">I'm also a book blogger: <a href="https://vee-bookish.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Vee_Bookish</a><br /><br />Honestly, this book made slogging through the first two worth it. While Mary and Gabry (Annah's twin sister) spend most of their time whining and letting everyone else fix things for them, Annah seemed much more independent after being left in the Dark City by Elias three years ago. She's by far my favourite character of the three girls and really made the read worthwhile, particularly towards the final pages.<br /><br />Elias and Gabry did not come across as well however. There was one particularly memorable scene where Annah asks Gabry how she's okay with Elias essentially handing over people to be tortured to death and she's like... Yeah but the dick is really good *shrug* Plus Elias decided that fucking off and leaving a teenage girl in a city with no law enforcement and a fuck ton of zombies was actually an okay idea.<br /><br />We spend most of our time on an island of soldiers trying not to get raped, which was just lovely. It did give some good bonding moments between Gabry and Annah, and Catcher and Annah which I did really enjoy. The first and last parts of the book were quite fast paced and binge worthy, but the middle did slog.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Seriously though they sewed together a ton of old blankets and yeeted themselves out of there via hot air balloon and you expect me to buy that one without blinking a few times <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_156301383" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/156301383" />
    <a title="Ashlie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4478856-ashlie"><img alt="Ashlie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453869984p2/4478856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/156301383?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashlie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashlie" href="/user/show/4478856-ashlie">Ashlie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4478856-ashlie?shelf=favorite-reads-of-2011">favorite-reads-of-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer156301383" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18262036268703828914"><br/>What would you do if you knew you only had a few more days to live? What are you living for if the Unconsecrated swarm the earth in hoards, claiming any and all life they can come in contact with? Do you get sick of fighting and running, always surviving just to survive, doing whatever it takes to survive? Carrie Ryan sends all these questions (and much more!) through your mind with the final book in her Forest of Hands and Teeth trilogy, The Dark and Hollow Places.<br/><br/>This book was an amazing finis</span>
  <span id="freeText18262036268703828914" style="display:none"><br />What would you do if you knew you only had a few more days to live? What are you living for if the Unconsecrated swarm the earth in hoards, claiming any and all life they can come in contact with? Do you get sick of fighting and running, always surviving just to survive, doing whatever it takes to survive? Carrie Ryan sends all these questions (and much more!) through your mind with the final book in her Forest of Hands and Teeth trilogy, The Dark and Hollow Places.<br /><br />This book was an amazing finish to such a remarkable series. I love a writer who gives you something, say, a present, wrapped in pretty pink paper. This gift is so amazing, and the author allows it to grow in your heart, then rips it right back out, roughs it up some, okay, roughs it up A LOT, and then hands it back to you, wrapped in pretty new paper and says, "okay, this time you can have it. Maybe." That is what reading this book is like. I adored it. I adored the torture that some scenes were, the humanity that the characters attempt to preserve and the love that perseveres through all hopelessness.<br /><br />Another thing that is SO great about this trilogy is how each book is told from a different (and possibly new) character's POV, yet they are all intertwined so deeply, and rooted to each other. I love that each book introduces new characters and man, do the characters in these books ROCK YOUR FACE OFF. I loved how Annah tried to learn what she was really fight for and how Catcher tried to learn to be unbroken. Everything on the surface was about survival, but underneath is was so, so SO much deeper. Gabry and Elias were great complimentary characters whereas, in the volume before this book, The Dead-Tossed Waves, they really were the show. Their back story was plenty strong enough to allow them to reinforce the third books plot without rehashing too much of the plot of the series in TDAHP.<br /><br />I am grateful that authors like Carrie Ryan exist to torture us; it expands our horizons and thoughts in different ways. It doesn't always give us the "fairy-tale ending" but it helps to show us how adversity can create opportunities for us and reshape the way we see things. Just because something is different, doesn't mean it's bad. This book is SUCH a great example of that. Even though as a reader I flt hopelessness and despair during the course of events in this book, the characters never stopped hoping and believing that a better way existed. They knew it didn't have to be perfect, but that if they didn't just have to keep "surviving," they could really, truly live.<br /><br />I've never been into "zombie drama" stories or movies, but Carrie Ryan takes the undead to a whole new level. I love the suspense, the horror, the romance that makes surviving not just a matter of saving your own life, but of someone else's, and every other emotion and feeling this book (and series) evokes. This series is one of the best I've ever read and it absolutely graces the top of my "Favorite Series" list. Even if you think you don't like zombie stories, you need to read this series. If you were a fan of Forest of Hands and Teeth and The Dead-Tossed Waves, then I don't know why you're reading this review and not reading The Dark and Hollow Places. <br /><br />If you don't read this book, I hear you turn into a Mudo. Sucks to be yooooooou....<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18262036268703828914" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13504911923687346673">This final(?) volume in the series was more of the same. The world has ended, there are a few survivors trying to scrabble out an increasingly difficult and futile existence, and of course, the teenagers are smarter, faster and better than the adults. <br/><br/>More so than the other two books, the teenagers in <i>The Dark and Hollow Places</i>, were cast as "good," and the adults were unrelentingly bad, obstructionist, and in some cases, plain old vanilla stupid. <br/><br/>Still, I felt like I had to finish the series, a</span>
  <span id="freeText13504911923687346673" style="display:none">This final(?) volume in the series was more of the same. The world has ended, there are a few survivors trying to scrabble out an increasingly difficult and futile existence, and of course, the teenagers are smarter, faster and better than the adults. <br /><br />More so than the other two books, the teenagers in <i>The Dark and Hollow Places</i>, were cast as "good," and the adults were unrelentingly bad, obstructionist, and in some cases, plain old vanilla stupid. <br /><br />Still, I felt like I had to finish the series, and find out what happened to Gabry/Abigail from the book 2 cliffhanger. Fortunately, it's a quick and easy read, even if Annah's continual whining about her scars, and Catcher's "heat" got really old after about 50 pages. <br /><br />Not especially recommended, but if you've read this far, you might as well finish the series. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17171339625762478944"><b>OMG! No gif can describe my feelings after reading this book.<br/><br/>First impression: The second book was better, come onnn. Second impression: The Death-Tossed Waves disappointed, this is Champion! Dear Lord!</b><br/><br/>In Dark and Hollow Places is the main heroine Annah, the twin of Abigail which we all know as Gabry from The Death-Tossed Waves. Annah lives in a Dark City where she's waiting for his friend Elias, whom had fled from the village. A Few years ago he left to join the crimps for a couple of years to </span>
  <span id="freeText17171339625762478944" style="display:none"><b>OMG! No gif can describe my feelings after reading this book.<br /><br />First impression: The second book was better, come onnn. Second impression: The Death-Tossed Waves disappointed, this is Champion! Dear Lord!</b><br /><br />In Dark and Hollow Places is the main heroine Annah, the twin of Abigail which we all know as Gabry from The Death-Tossed Waves. Annah lives in a Dark City where she's waiting for his friend Elias, whom had fled from the village. A Few years ago he left to join the crimps for a couple of years to provide the service themselves and Anna safe, but it doesn't return for a long time and Annah isn't going to wait any longer. She decides to retire from the dangerous city and find a better life somewhere far away. It was at her departure but she sees his sister on the way to the city, so she stayed. Everything happens next will start the chain of events leading to a huge denouement: <i> Can the human race survive in the final battle against unclean (or whatever)?</i><br /><br />Yes, this book offers a huge finale. It is full of action, emotion and also is boasting my favorite heroine of this series. But the biggest plus is somewhere else. How dark and catastrophic this book is. One might expect it by name, but I guess no one can prepare to future like this only based on name. How far Carrie Ryan chased her vision of the Dark City really surprised me. <br /><br />As I said, Annah is my favorite heroine from this series. She's strong, harsh and brave. Even here, however, appear Carrie's shortcomings of previous books. Annah is too much thinking sometimes. She's still discussing her guilt she feels towards his sister (I survived that, yay!) but she's still discussing her feelings for boys. Yes, there's a love triangle AGAIN, although now it's more like a <b>square.</b> As we know, Gabry was dating Catcher, but she fell in love with Elias after his transformation. Well, Annah was in love with Elias, but the more she was recognized Catcher, the more she was detached of that feelings (especially when he licked her twin)and, of course, she begins to discuss her growing feelings for Catcher. And here we go...<br /><br /><b>I didn't like Catcher very much. I noticed one thing in this series - when there are two boys in one book, one is good and a second is bad, literally literally as BAD. He's rude, mad. And in this book I found that Catcher isn't that bad, neither rude or mad. Maybe he's more attractive than Elias. And that scene when he was crying and hugging Annah in her bed was just ohhh...O:-) </b><br /><br />Fearful caution on the topic of sex. Little spoiler - I think that last night of Anna and Elias, before he joined the crimps. Did you also thought that they, as it were, came to the last base? Were you also surprised that they were just ''kissing''? Because Annah Although can undress to the waist ahead of Catcher (left her pants and shoes) or take his hands and put them on her breasts, but God forbid that they were doing something more than kissing and making out together! You know what? Bullshit.<br /><br />Well, that's just something I noticed and want to get out of my head. When I let out that love triangle (square) and thinking about the past, it was really great book and super ending of this series. I really enjoyed Dark and Hollow Places and it's just a pity that there are no more books similar to this one!<br /></span>

<div id="review_98443397" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/98443397" />
    <a title="Nely" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1440151-nely"><img alt="Nely" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1271166357p2/1440151.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/98443397?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nely" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nely" href="/user/show/1440151-nely">Nely</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1440151-nely?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1440151-nely?shelf=autographed">autographed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer98443397" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11711571513620333568">In the third and final installment in her Forest of Hands and Teeth series, Carrie Ryan, introduces you to Annah. Annah has been living on her own in the Dark City since Elias left to join the protectorate. With scars that mar her face and body, Annah is more of a recluse. She uses her street smarts - bowing her head, not making eye contact and blending into the shadows as a weapon. Without any friends or family she has used these skills as a way to survive the dangers of the Dark City. Waiting </span>
  <span id="freeText11711571513620333568" style="display:none">In the third and final installment in her Forest of Hands and Teeth series, Carrie Ryan, introduces you to Annah. Annah has been living on her own in the Dark City since Elias left to join the protectorate. With scars that mar her face and body, Annah is more of a recluse. She uses her street smarts - bowing her head, not making eye contact and blending into the shadows as a weapon. Without any friends or family she has used these skills as a way to survive the dangers of the Dark City. Waiting for Elias, her life has become as lifeless as that of the Unconsecrated but then she meets Catcher. Catcher who brings with him memories of a past that she has longed to forget.<br /><br />Out of the three leading ladies you will find in this series, Annah was hands down my favorite. She wasn't a whiner like Mary, and Gabry annoyed me with all her boy drama... but Annah was phenomenal. She was tough as nails, brave, strong and courageous. Her will to live was a breath of fresh air. Even though she's scarred, feels alone and even broken at times - she still was not willing to give up. <br /><br />Out of the three books I believe this was the darkest one. Their struggle for survival was the most intense. I went through a slew of emotions from sadness, hopelessness, and even found myself choked up more than once. I can't even imagine a life this bleak where the unconsecrated are a threat but humans can be just as dangerous. <br /><br />Yet through it all I found myself hopeful. I found myself waiting for and really savoring the moments that weren't as dark... moments of light. Especially when those moments dealt with Annah and Catcher's relationship. The fact that they are both so broken and flawed really makes you hope that they can find a way to make it work in a world infested by the living dead. Originally, I was worried that I wouldn't like this final installment since I was so focused on Gabry and Elias's story (The Dead-Tossed Waves) but I think Ms. Ryan did a wonderful job in connecting everything together. <br /><br />Overall this book was incredible. The whole series is amazing. Full of tension, suspense, nail-biting action and Unconsecrated... lots and lots of Unconsecrated. I can't recommend it enough!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11711571513620333568" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_149814990" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/149814990" />
    <a title="★ Jess " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2683062-jess"><img alt="★ Jess " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466182835p2/2683062.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/149814990?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer149814990" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer16595848913601494344">Hands down the <b>best</b> book I have read this year, and easily the strongest installment of this trilogy-which is now my second favorite of all time, second to only<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/44939-chaos-walking' rel='nofollow noopener'>"Chaos Walking"</a> <br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3432478.The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth__The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth___1_' title='The Forest of Hands and Teeth (The Forest of Hands and Teeth, #1) by Carrie Ryan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Forest of Hands and Teeth</a> was worth 4.5 stars <br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6555517.The_Dead_Tossed_Waves__The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth___2_' title='The Dead-Tossed Waves (The Forest of Hands and Teeth, #2) by Carrie Ryan' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dead-Tossed Waves</a> was worth 4 stars <br/>This finale is worth almost six.
