The descriptions & image</span>
  <span id="freeText16595848913601494344" style="display:none">Hands down the <b>best</b> book I have read this year, and easily the strongest installment of this trilogy-which is now my second favorite of all time, second to only<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/44939-chaos-walking" rel="nofollow noopener">"Chaos Walking"</a> <br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3432478.The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth__The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth___1_" title="The Forest of Hands and Teeth (The Forest of Hands and Teeth, #1) by Carrie Ryan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Forest of Hands and Teeth</a> was worth 4.5 stars <br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6555517.The_Dead_Tossed_Waves__The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth___2_" title="The Dead-Tossed Waves (The Forest of Hands and Teeth, #2) by Carrie Ryan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dead-Tossed Waves</a> was worth 4 stars <br />This finale is worth almost six. It was magnificent. <br /><br />It takes place in a dying New York City, at least 200 years into the future. This is now called "The Dark City"-one of the last safe places on a dead earth. The descriptions &amp; imagery that Carrie Ryan uses throughout the book is magnificent-some images I will never be able to remove from my mind-both beautiful &amp; terribly haunting at the same time: <br />-The dead and rotting New York skyline at dawn, with a handful of fires flickering in each building , being one of the said images. <br />I typed six more, but all of them were mega-spoilers, and thats not on. <br /><br />The third book is narrated by a third protagonist-Annah, and she is the most likable and interesting yet. <br />Everything I type will not do justice to this thrilling book...so yeah. Just read it. <br />Its written well, paced terrifically, the characters are wonderful and the dark atmosphere is sensational. I just wanted to pull Annah out of the book and comfort her. <br />And the ending...oh wow. I am considering making a goodreads shelf for 'best climaxes' just for this book. <br />I LOVE EVERYTHING ABOUT THIS SOOOO MUCH! <br /><br />Ive tried recommending this series to my friends, but they just scoff: "Zombies...thats so stupid!"<br />But no, its not. The zombies/unconcencrated/Mudo/Plauge Rats are not the base of this story. Its all about human nature, survival, love -and mostly: the power of hope. <br /><br />Please, please, please, please: <br />Read this trilogy. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16595848913601494344" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=monsters">monsters</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer156582094" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2642520956843511349">Argh, Carrie Ryan. Such a good writer, and yet there's always something about her books that bothers me. Last time, in Dead-Tossed Waves, I was bored by both the heroine and the romance. This is an improvement, in that it's just the romance that bothered me.<br/><br/>Gabry honestly irritated me, so I was not exactly looking forward to a book from the POV of her sister. Luckily, Annah is a far more interesting character, rather more like Mary had been: flawed, and not always perfectly likable, but an inter</span>
  <span id="freeText2642520956843511349" style="display:none">Argh, Carrie Ryan. Such a good writer, and yet there's always something about her books that bothers me. Last time, in Dead-Tossed Waves, I was bored by both the heroine and the romance. This is an improvement, in that it's just the romance that bothered me.<br /><br />Gabry honestly irritated me, so I was not exactly looking forward to a book from the POV of her sister. Luckily, Annah is a far more interesting character, rather more like Mary had been: flawed, and not always perfectly likable, but an interesting person anyways. Ryan's setting and creep factor remain as good as ever. It's just that romance.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Let me break down what happens in the romance: Elias and Annah grow up as brother and sister. At some point, she falls into a barbed wire fence and becomes heavily scarred over half her body, which understandably gives her some issues. Elias and Annah (who have, I remind you, been brother and sister for years) start to fall in love, which isn't squicky <i>at all</i>. However, Elias decides that he doesn't want to deal with Annah's issues and runs off. While away, he meets Gabry, Annah's identical twin sister. Who has no scars. Cue insta-love on his part. I don't think I need to elaborate on how much this bothered me. But wait, it's not over yet! Early in the book, Elias, Gabry, Annah, and Catcher meet up. In the prior book, Gabry had rejected Catcher in favor of Elias. But then he meets Annah, identical to Gabry save the scars, and boom! Insta-love. It's appallingly obvious that Catcher is using her as a stand-in for Gabry, at least at first. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> It might be possible for a writer to work me past my initial distaste for this entire love rhombus, but Ryan doesn't do the heavy lifting.<br /><br />This is why Carrie Ryan drives me crazy. Her books are almost entirely really good, but there's always just one thing that bugs me. It's to her credit that I even attempted to finish this book at all, much less that I enjoyed it as much as I did. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2642520956843511349" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1442318236" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1021364693900373876"><b>That sad part when you don't follow your instincts and DNF a book.</b><br/><br/>Annah is scarred inside out. She abandoned her twin sister several years ago to the Unconsecrated (zombies) and has since survived with various scars all over her body and face. But now, that her sister is found, Annah starts developing other feelings such as jealousy and lover boy envy. Can Annah ever be at peace? <br/><br/>Despite being the third book in the series, Ryan chose to focus the story on a new character with a dull personality.</span>
  <span id="freeText1021364693900373876" style="display:none"><b>That sad part when you don't follow your instincts and DNF a book.</b><br /><br />Annah is scarred inside out. She abandoned her twin sister several years ago to the Unconsecrated (zombies) and has since survived with various scars all over her body and face. But now, that her sister is found, Annah starts developing other feelings such as jealousy and lover boy envy. Can Annah ever be at peace? <br /><br />Despite being the third book in the series, Ryan chose to focus the story on a new character with a dull personality. Not only is Annah constantly conflicted, but her reasoning makes little sense. She immediately sees her sister after years of guilt, and feels nothing but jealousy. Admits to loving Elias, only to flirt with Catcher right away. It's impossible to root for a character that doesn't know what she wants. <br /><br />The action is also constantly stalled, as our four main characters are being held under their will. Together they must decide if they desire to live or exist (tough existentialist question during apocalyptic zombie times).<br /><br />Wish Ryan would have stopped at book two. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1021364693900373876" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_647051736" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/647051736" />
    <a title="Amy Nielsen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1271874-amy-nielsen"><img alt="Amy Nielsen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1377003691p2/1271874.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/647051736?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy Nielsen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy Nielsen" href="/user/show/1271874-amy-nielsen">Amy Nielsen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1271874-amy-nielsen?shelf=never-again">never-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1271874-amy-nielsen?shelf=paranormal-suspense">paranormal-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1271874-amy-nielsen?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1271874-amy-nielsen?shelf=obnoxious">obnoxious</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1271874-amy-nielsen?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1271874-amy-nielsen?shelf=2013-booklist">2013-booklist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1271874-amy-nielsen?shelf=waste-of-time">waste-of-time</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1271874-amy-nielsen?shelf=i_just_dont_know_what_to_say">i_just_dont_know_what_to_say</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer647051736" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer762086470313003994">Where oh where do we begin? The ONLY reason I continued beyond book 2 was that I hoped beyond hope that something awesome might happen and somehow this crew would whip the zombie's butts and create a new world. Well, since I gave up on this book in the last 20 minutes of it (audiobook), it's not looking like that happened, unless it happened super fast. No, I wouldn't have normally given up that close to the end but my library loan ended and I just don't care what finally happened to stupid Anna</span>
  <span id="freeText762086470313003994" style="display:none">Where oh where do we begin? The ONLY reason I continued beyond book 2 was that I hoped beyond hope that something awesome might happen and somehow this crew would whip the zombie's butts and create a new world. Well, since I gave up on this book in the last 20 minutes of it (audiobook), it's not looking like that happened, unless it happened super fast. No, I wouldn't have normally given up that close to the end but my library loan ended and I just don't care what finally happened to stupid Annah in the tunnels in the frigid air. Yes, say frigid air out loud and see if you don't laugh out loud. Because I heard it repeatedly like 7 times and I was like, wha? what is she talking about a refrigerator for? I understand the air is cold, but is this author so completely devoid of imagination that the only words she can use to describe cold air repeatedly is frigid air?<br /><br />Stupid similes, something is always "like" something else in a totally long-winded annoying way. The stupid self-talk continues as in the other books and random bits of tedious unimportant information that is forever fed to the reader. This is not good literature - it is annoying fluff. <br /><br />Annah is a self-pitying reject who has no original idea of her own and trusts no one and yet falls in love with Catcher without any real reason that I can see. Let's talk about Catcher for a second though. This is a boy as 2 dimensional as the pages of the book. This boy is totally into Annah's twin sister for all of book 2 and decides he can't be with her because it's too big of a risk. And yet, 1 day later (okay maybe a week later) he meets Gabry's twin sister, scarred and broken, and falls in love too - again, with no reason that is made clear to us. And yet although Annah is Gabry's twin, she's the ugly twin. But Catcher's willing to sacrifice all of his scruples for the ugly twin - and not even the nice ugly twin. She's the mean, ugly twin. I don't get this 2 dimensional stuff. And so we don't get enough information as to why the relationships go in the directions they do, and yet we know exactly minute inconsequential events occur. <br /><br />Here are a few examples of extraneous sentences that tell us nothing and waste space:<br /><br />1) My heart's pounding so furiously that I don't know if it will ever calm down again. (steller lit there)<br />2) I'm punching and screaming and kicking and twisting and fighting as...[really, because i thought you were having a peaceful stroll] - are there no better words to describe the fact that she's fighting back? and and and. please.<br />3) I'm so focused on on the Recruiters that I don't notice another body slip into the room. I don't notice him make his way along the edge of the wall. (this constant repeating of the same phrase is so prevalent in this book - redundancy for the sake of making an impression is poor writing IMHO).<br /><br />And the partial sentences are so grating (ya partial sentence intended). I can't stand poor grammar from an author. If you are going to write, please don't insult my intelligence by using poor grammar. There is no excuse. It is not cool, trendy or whatever it is you're hoping to achieve. It just makes you look like a marginal amateur author.<br /><br />Last but not least, the narrator for this book was terrible. She made all of the author's flaws 100% more apparent. I know this because I went onto Google Books and looked up the book so I could actually read it, and it wasn't quite so bad. Which tells me that the narrator was an amateur too. Please blow your nose before you read - ya, really.<br /><br />*SPOILER*<br /><br />I know that other people gave this book and the 2 before it really good reviews. But frankly I am more discerning with my spare time and I feel like I just wasted it. I look back over the 3 books and feel like so very little of any monument actually happened and the end of book 3 was a joke - how convenient that a group of completely untrained "children" could come up with such a viable option and create this complex aircraft for their escape. Made from quilts and oil? It didn't burn up? No trial run? Right. It makes about as much sense as the whole rest of this ridiculous series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="762086470313003994" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review647051736">

<div id="review_1345495467" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1345495467" />
    <a title="Dani ❤️ Perspective of a Writer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer"><img alt="Dani ❤️ Perspective of a Writer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1553042105p2/7476091.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1345495467?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dani ❤️ Perspective of a Writer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dani ❤️ Perspective of a Writer" href="/user/show/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer">Dani ❤️ Perspective of a Writer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Readers of the 1st 2 books.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=fiction-young-adult">fiction-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=g-r-zombies">g-r-zombies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=g-t-future">g-t-future</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=genre-romance-deliberately">genre-romance-deliberately</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=series-book-3-plus">series-book-3-plus</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=g-c-other-places">g-c-other-places</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=imo-worthy-love-interest">imo-worthy-love-interest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=genre-dystopian">genre-dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7476091-dani-perspective-of-a-writer?shelf=stars-3">stars-3</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1345495467" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer468081794215970299">A dystopian sci-fi story spanning three books about life after several generations of zombie occupation set in the New York City area at a time when humans are barely holding on. This is the 3rd installment told by yet another young woman, connected to both of the previous narrators. I'm so grateful to be done with this series. The first two books made me want to tear my hair out! They were imaginative for a well worn trope yet I disliked the narrators intensely. For the first time I felt like t</span>
  <span id="freeText468081794215970299" style="display:none">A dystopian sci-fi story spanning three books about life after several generations of zombie occupation set in the New York City area at a time when humans are barely holding on. This is the 3rd installment told by yet another young woman, connected to both of the previous narrators. I'm so grateful to be done with this series. The first two books made me want to tear my hair out! They were imaginative for a well worn trope yet I disliked the narrators intensely. For the first time I felt like the right character was picked for the point of view of the story.<br /><br />Yeah, I liked Annah. She did whine a little, but I think that was a "reality" the author chose to include. While I disagree with the choice, it is her choice to make. I'm not a fan of how information about their past is dissimulated to the reader. I'd have started with the scars. They really make Annah unique more than any other point in her backstory. Yes, she did something horrible to her sister and she had a boy she liked posing as her brother but the scars are a history only she can relate to. It makes her stand out. Instead of "showing" her whining about how people treat her, actually show her using her scars as armor. Still for all the flaws in her author, I really liked Annah. She'd had a tough life, full of sorrow and regret and yet she'd learned survival. She tried to make good decisions in the midst of really bad situations and wasn't always successful but did her damnedest. I can admire such moxie.<br /><br />I really, really liked Catcher for her. I feel like Catcher deserved to be happy and he understood better than Elias all that she'd been through and why she was the tough girl she is now. There were a lot more sensical to the character storylines surrounding Annah too than the other books. There is dealing with the guilt and jealousy toward her returned sister. There is the lost potential of her love for her one and only loved one Elias who has moved on to the sister. Also Catcher is not a "catch" he is a very damaged young man who will be a constant support and danger for Annah the rest of her life. There is also the situation that Elias got them all into with his pessimism about the state of the world. It's all a bit of a stretch to me but imaginative in a way.<br /><br />I enjoyed the emotional journeys the best. Gabry suddenly became an emotionally stable, strong young woman in this book and I applaud the change even as I note that this is NOT the same young woman from The Dead-Tossed Waves (though no time has passed). I liked the experiences she shared with Annah - supporting Annah and giving Annah a reason to hope that not all relationships are as doomed as the world. I also appreciate Annah coming to terms with what happened with Elias. He too is not the same young man we met and we learn than he's actually not nearly the mysterious savior he appeared to be so much a rather selfish ass. And last but not least that she comes to understand it's not how long you live that makes you human but HOW you live! All this is ruined by the fantastical ending. I won't ruin it in the least, but while the "pushing into a brutal state of affairs" was well pushed the "extraditing from said state of affairs" was not as believable. And as always the motives and reasoning of the characters is totally wonky. I've learned to simply "overlook" character consistency in this series.<br /><br />BOTTOM LINE: This is the story that the first book of the series should have been.<br /><br /><br />*Mild Spoilers*<br /><br />The villains were a joke. Annah did better facing her own demons and the trial of their situation than facing these jokers. They were the fodder for the middle of the story to occupy the time while she thought of how to escape. Ox bull-headedly sticking to his men, when it would have been better for him to switch sides to Catcher when he saw the way of things. Or thin out his men...less to feed and use them as an example. And his second in command...*shakes head* Just very flat evil and mindbogglingly neutral.</span>
  <a data-text-id="468081794215970299" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2610193979" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2610193979" />
    <a title="Amelia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10715206-amelia"><img alt="Amelia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525024983p2/10715206.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2610193979?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amelia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amelia" href="/user/show/10715206-amelia">Amelia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780575094840" href="/book/show/12885279-the-dark-and-hollow-places">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10715206-amelia?shelf=love-triangulitis">love-triangulitis</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10715206-amelia?shelf=amazingwhatyoufindincharityshops">amazingwhatyoufindincharityshops</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10715206-amelia?shelf=physical-copy">physical-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10715206-amelia?shelf=childrens-and-young-adult">childrens-and-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10715206-amelia?shelf=instalove">instalove</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2610193979" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2509889678493442469">Well, it wasn't terrible. Contrary to the critical review ahead, I did actually like some parts: Annah's painting/drawing, particularly when she paints a portrait of an infected woman with the remnants of makeup that she left behind. Catcher, too. He who was quite the noble-hearted soul and deserved much more page time, perhaps à la <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15842439.Warm_Bodies__Warm_Bodies___1_' title='Warm Bodies (Warm Bodies, #1) by Isaac Marion' rel='nofollow noopener'>Warm Bodies</a>. He'd've been a much better protagonist. <br/><br/>This review will be a mixture of my thoughts on <i>The Dark and Hollow Places </i> and on the series as a whole. <br/><br/>I thin</span>
  <span id="freeText2509889678493442469" style="display:none">Well, it wasn't terrible. Contrary to the critical review ahead, I did actually like some parts: Annah's painting/drawing, particularly when she paints a portrait of an infected woman with the remnants of makeup that she left behind. Catcher, too. He who was quite the noble-hearted soul and deserved much more page time, perhaps à la <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15842439.Warm_Bodies__Warm_Bodies___1_" title="Warm Bodies (Warm Bodies, #1) by Isaac Marion" rel="nofollow noopener">Warm Bodies</a>. He'd've been a much better protagonist. <br /><br />This review will be a mixture of my thoughts on <i>The Dark and Hollow Places </i> and on the series as a whole. <br /><br />I think perhaps the author would've done better to have written this story for an adult audience. The series features some potentially pretty horrific things: the threat of being eaten alive, of losing yourself, of starving to death, of having to behead someone who once loved you and now has turned against you, and the omnipresent fear for women in war zones: rape. But this is all tackled lightly - or rather, "lite"-ly. It's weak and I never felt any major concern for the characters. We had these clear YA romance plots: a fair bit of instalove, no real fear of death. <br /><br />I don't know if it's because I'm not a young adult anymore, or because life doesn't let many people keep their naïvety but I had no patience for Annah and Gabry's sanctimonious shit. Gabry tearfully confesses to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[killing a man who was effectively going to rape her <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and hopes that Annah won't think she's a terrible person. Does Annah tell her she was entirely justified, WHICH SHE WAS? Nope! And when Catcher <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[kills a soldier enjoying bloodsports, that he was going to make Annah take part in <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, she says it was murder and that they have to be better people. Are you fucking kidding me??? I hate it when characters put their philosophising before their basic survival instinct. <br /><br />I'm also no longer willing to forgive simplistic plotting. I mentioned this in my review for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6555517.The_Dead_Tossed_Waves__The_Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth___2_" title="The Dead-Tossed Waves (The Forest of Hands and Teeth, #2) by Carrie Ryan" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dead-Tossed Waves</a>, but honestly - yes, it's a pretty image, survivors floating away from the zombie hoardes in <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[patchwork hot air balloons <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> but it needed more work. How did they steer, for one? And why <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[weren't there any zombies there when they all landed? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Do any of them actually know how to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[control a ship? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />But before all of that - how did Mary get back to Vista? And why did they let her in? How did Annah survive for years on her own in a city - lately with no law but the military - without being violated? Without having to defend herself with force? Without shedding some innocence? And why was it effective, our little gang of refugees choosing a tower block home, hoping that their captors wouldn't bother to climb the stairs to mess with them? Let's be realistic here: two young women, a whole island full of men caged, frustrated, bored, facing the end of the world, with no real prospect of ever seeing any other uninfected women again, basically just waiting to die... Ryan, do you seriously believe that a few flights of stairs would be enough of a deterrent?<br /><br />I didn't mean for rape to be such a focus of my review. I just... if I'm going to read <s>post</s> apocalyptic fiction, I expect to see some realism. And if you're going to touch on difficult subjects, you have to do them justice. I know that that's harder to achieve given the restraints of YA, but it's not impossible. I'd like to see more YA authors take page space up on building a world and characters who are shaped by it than on making sure every character experiences a romance.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2509889678493442469" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_159618652" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/159618652" />
    <a title="Greta is Erikasbuddy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3267545-greta-is-erikasbuddy"><img alt="Greta is Erikasbuddy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1389224768p2/3267545.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/159618652?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Greta is Erikasbuddy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Greta is Erikasbuddy" href="/user/show/3267545-greta-is-erikasbuddy">Greta is Erikasbuddy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer159618652" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17741736188391677296">I adore this series.<br/> <br/>I was skeptical at first but I always am. I just can't hand the lip gloss dot your eyes with wash and curl kind of books.<br/> <br/>This series isn't one of them. <br/> <br/>These books made me squee with delight as each girl endured a loss sprikled torture but found love in the most unsuspecting of places.<br/> <br/>I loved the insert zombie here and make it a bit rougher than your normal hard knock life kinda story. It was a very interesting world. Dare I say better than Harry Potter? I actually do say</span>
  <span id="freeText17741736188391677296" style="display:none">I adore this series.<br /> <br />I was skeptical at first but I always am. I just can't hand the lip gloss dot your eyes with wash and curl kind of books.<br /> <br />This series isn't one of them. <br /> <br />These books made me squee with delight as each girl endured a loss sprikled torture but found love in the most unsuspecting of places.<br /> <br />I loved the insert zombie here and make it a bit rougher than your normal hard knock life kinda story. It was a very interesting world. Dare I say better than Harry Potter? I actually do say because I know Hogwarts would never accept me but the Forest would welcome me with open arms, the Waves would try to take me away, and those Hollow Places would be a nice blanket when I tried to hide my head. Plus, I'm one of those weirdos who could never get into the Potter books.<br /> <br />--- that's not really telling you what the book is about, is it?<br /> <br /><br /><br /><br />Well, I'd like to tell you everything. I really would, but you see... it would totally wreck the first 2 books for you if you haven't read them.<br /> <br />So, to those who have read the series: I really enjoyed what I read.<br /> <br />To those of you who haven't read the series: I highly recommend it. I would have loved to have read a series like this when I was thirteen and up (I'm sure a 12 year old could handle it but there are some graphic violence that parents might want to censor till the child gets a bit older and won't wind up in their bed when the wind rattles the tree branch against their window-- FYI: TEETH scared me so bad that I thought my house was infested with zombies for a time lolz)<br /> <br /><br /><br /><br />I enjoyed this series way more than the Beautiful one. It's about neck and neck with the Iron one but that's only because both of those worlds are just so different and unique that they tie in different ways. The originality of the zombie apocalypse has been done before but the plot was one of a kind and very imaginative. I also enjoyed how each book was done by a different girl's point of view. That really wowed me. The way the author linked everyone up but made each story different was amazing.<br /> <br />I have to admit that this is NOT a stand-alone book. If you picked up "DARK" you could probably get away from reading "TEETH" but you could NOT get away from reading "WAVES". I had a hard time remembering what happened in the second book so I recommend reading WAVES and DARK back to back if you can. IF you can't it is fine. THe stories that you might not remember are explained to you but you'll be brain farting for a while until then. (I know I was).<br /> <br />I now want to read all the short anthology stories that have been written in this land. I want to disect this world a little more. While I am sad that this was the final book I am very satisfied with the way that it ended. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />-song that I kept thinking of throughout the book: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=HLL6ON18vGI">http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=HLL6ON...</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17741736188391677296" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_168645194" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/168645194" />
    <a title="Duchess Nicole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2204947-duchess-nicole"><img alt="Duchess Nicole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499265843p2/2204947.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/168645194?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Duchess Nicole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Duchess Nicole" href="/user/show/2204947-duchess-nicole">Duchess Nicole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=genre-ya">genre-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=e-pcs">e-pcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=genre-ya-dystopian">genre-ya-dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2204947-duchess-nicole?shelf=zombies">zombies</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer168645194" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17349589278146541367">I feel like I’ve been through an emotional wringer for the last two evenings. If you’re looking for a feel good zombie book with a happy ending to the horror filled flesh eating monster series, do not look here. At no point in the reading of this entire series have I ever had happy feelings. <br/><br/>That being said, this is a series that will stay with me for the rest of my life. Maybe I shelter myself with romance too often. In my endless search for literary escape, do I miss out on these thought provo</span>
  <span id="freeText17349589278146541367" style="display:none">I feel like I’ve been through an emotional wringer for the last two evenings. If you’re looking for a feel good zombie book with a happy ending to the horror filled flesh eating monster series, do not look here. At no point in the reading of this entire series have I ever had happy feelings. <br /><br />That being said, this is a series that will stay with me for the rest of my life. Maybe I shelter myself with romance too often. In my endless search for literary escape, do I miss out on these thought provoking gems? Even if that’s the case, I just don’t think I could handle the gut wrenching hopelessness that permeates the Forest of Hands and Teeth series. I don’t really want to think of how I would react to the last days of my life, or what I would do if my husband or heaven forbid, children…tried to eat me. <br /><br />Ms Ryan is an amazing author. Truly, the thoughts she must have in her head to be able to come up with this entire world, the characterization and imagery that she creates is stunning. No matter how much I say I don’t ever read this type of book, I have to give props to her. She is an artist with words, painting a vivid dystopian society that feels so real! I swear I heard moans coming from my front porch, and New York City really IS being swallowed by the horde of Unconsecrated. Someone better check on that.<br /><br />What would humanity do if they were in this situation? Is this what people turn into? Those in power preying on the weak, building cities just so they can control, rape, murder? It’s a scary world to live in, and I’m so very angry that the bad guys don’t get what they deserve. The torture that they dish out is atrocious. They prey on the weak, and Anna’s inner good girl made me want to shake her. Doesn’t she deserve justice? Don’t the other victims deserve some form of retribution? Buck up, little girl! The horrors taking place around you, the inhumanity of the humans who are meant to protect you needs to stop! That bothered me more than anything else.<br /><br />The ending, I’m sure everyone knows by now, if they’ve read any other reviews, is wholly dissatisfying. I felt like Mrs. Ryan just…got tired of writing escape attempts. So she tack on a paragraph or two that screams “THE END” and left it at that. Don’t her readers DESERVE some form of happy? Or at the very least some sort of finality? Something, ANYTHING to give us a hint as to what this struggle has all been for? No, we don’t. I wish we did. I could have given this the fifth star. As it is, I’m so very angry right now that I can’t think straight. I want to rant and rant and pitch a fit. But I shall refrain and move on with my life. I almost hope there isn’t another book, because I know I’d feel like I have to read it. How amazing that a person can bring out these emotions in so many readers. What a fabulous accomplishment and what a great job she did. Bravo to Carrie Ryan. Now write a freaking epilogue!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17349589278146541367" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_348047214" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/348047214" />
    <a title="Jon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4277731-jon"><img alt="Jon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1384212540p2/4277731.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/348047214?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jon" href="/user/show/4277731-jon">Jon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4277731-jon?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4277731-jon?shelf=dystopia-post-apocalyptic">dystopia-post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4277731-jon?shelf=zombies-brains">zombies-brains</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer348047214" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11946690808232588234"><a href='http://scottreadsit.blogspot.com/2013/04/the-dark-and-hollow-places-by-carrie.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Check out more reviews at Scott Reads It!</a><br/><b> <i> "Sometimes life isn't about the end. It's not always about tomorrow and the day after that-what we achieve over the years and how we leave the world. Sometimes it's about today."</i></b>  <br/> I was a bit reluctant to read The Dark And Hollow Places for two reasons. I have read tons of trilogies and the 3rd book in a trilogy almost always manages to disappoint me. I usually don't like how authors resolve trilogies because the conclusions usually feel way too rushed</span>
  <span id="freeText11946690808232588234" style="display:none"><a href="http://scottreadsit.blogspot.com/2013/04/the-dark-and-hollow-places-by-carrie.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Check out more reviews at Scott Reads It!</a><br /><b> <i> "Sometimes life isn't about the end. It's not always about tomorrow and the day after that-what we achieve over the years and how we leave the world. Sometimes it's about today."</i></b>  <br /> I was a bit reluctant to read The Dark And Hollow Places for two reasons. I have read tons of trilogies and the 3rd book in a trilogy almost always manages to disappoint me. I usually don't like how authors resolve trilogies because the conclusions usually feel way too rushed. Second of all, it sounds kind of juvenile but I avoided reading this book because I didn't want this series to end. The Dark And Hollow Places is an extremely satisfying conclusion that definitely exceeded all of my expectations.<br /><br /> Carrie Ryan is truly a literary genius. Only Carrie Ryan could make a zombie book into something so beautiful and emotionally powerful. The Dark And Hollow Places filled me with hope and yet at the same time it broke my heart and shattered it into a million pieces. No matter how hopeless a situation may seem, no situation is entirely hopeless. <br /><br /> Annah is so different from Mary and Gabry but I still loved her nevertheless. Annah is extremely insecure about herself but you really can't blame her. Some readers will probably find Annah irritating but her insecurity is really a result of her situation. Even though everything feels so bleak and hopeless, Annah is determined to continue to fight each and every day.If I was in the situation that Annah was, I highly doubt I'd be as hopeful or determined as she was. I really loved watching Annah evolve as a person and accept who she is. <br /><br /> The Dark And Hollow Places is even more horrifying than both The Forest And Hands Of Teeth and The Dead Tossed Waves. Everything feels even more bleak and hopeless in this book. Carrie Ryan takes advantage of the situation and uses the setting to put across some thought provoking messages. What does it mean to be human? When is it okay to give up? Is life worth living without hope? <br /><br /> Some people have complained about how this series ended because it's a bit open ended. I found the ending extremely satisfying and it was a truly perfect ending. I don't want to give anything way but I loved the ending!<br /><br /> The Dark And Hollow Places is a thought-provoking conclusion to one of my all-time favorite series. I really look forward to reading more of Carrie Ryan's books and I hope I enjoy them as much as I enjoyed this book. I'd highly recommend reading all of The Forest Of Hands And Teeth books and I believe these books really deserve the hype they receive!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11946690808232588234" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('P+iasxtbUXPgclFm9aLtkhSzaWYU/n03GRQ/C/cBFsQFzvNhoAWYG0dZ5QcCV+dNwuyOrtpz81BCanm6OkLkXg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZM8bpiDRCr+Xnjbj3MKDH4iTkPp4bTj1pCbl0SKVaE5e6XJ0m4/D1zC1goIrN4nAXsx3MrbgtpL/WKNg79aa1A==')})
  }

  <span id="freeText13054213538234415146" style="display:none">Carrie Ryan is the <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author of a lot of books. She use to be a lawyer. Happily, she is not anymore. You can keep it that way by reading her books:<br /><br />If you like zombies, try the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3432478._Forest_of_Hands_and_Teeth" title=" Forest of Hands and Teeth" rel="nofollow noopener"> Forest of Hands and Teeth</a> series.<br /><br />If you like clever, fun adventure fantasy for 8-12 year olds, definitely read the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20980662._Map_To_Everywhere" title=" Map To Everywhere" rel="nofollow noopener"> Map To Everywhere</a> series (co-written with her husband, John Parke Davis).<br /><br />If you like cold calculated revenge involving hidden identities and lots of secrets: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23281652._Daughter_of_Deep_Silence" title=" Daughter of Deep Silence" rel="nofollow noopener"> Daughter of Deep Silence</a>.<br /><br />If you or your kids like multi-author, multi-platform series like 39 Clues and Spirit Animals, try <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13356177._Infinity_Ring__Divide_and_Conquer" title=" Infinity Ring: Divide and Conquer" rel="nofollow noopener"> Infinity Ring: Divide and Conquer</a> -- it's produced by the same publisher (and has vikings and true history!)<br /><br />If you like true-crime stuff (both fiction and podcasts), <b>check out her upcoming release, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40490159._Dead_Air" title=" Dead Air" rel="nofollow noopener"> Dead Air</a>, a serialized thriller co-written with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1951011._Gwenda_Bond" title=" Gwenda Bond" rel="nofollow noopener"> Gwenda Bond</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15292._Rachel_Caine" title=" Rachel Caine" rel="nofollow noopener"> Rachel Caine</a>.</b><br /><br />If you're pretty sure you won't survive the zombie apocalypse, you're in good company. She won't either.<br /><br /><b>instagram:</b> <a href="https://www.instagram.com/carrieryanwrites/" rel="nofollow noopener">@CarrieRyanWrites</a><br /><b>twitter:</b> <a href="http://www.twitter.com/carrieryan" rel="nofollow noopener">@CarrieRyan</a><br /><b>website:</b> <a href="http://www.carrieryan.com" rel="nofollow noopener">www.CarrieRyan.com</a></span>
